	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Germanic name</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><p><a href="/wiki/Germanic_languages" title="Germanic languages">Germanic</a> <a href="/wiki/Given_name" title="Given name">given names</a> are traditionally <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/dithematic" class="extiw" title="wikt:dithematic">dithematic</a>; that is, they are formed from two elements, by joining a <a href="/wiki/Prefix" title="Prefix">prefix</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Suffix" title="Suffix">suffix</a>. For example, <a href="/wiki/Ethelred_II_of_England" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethelred II of England">King Æþelred</a>'s name was derived from <i><i lang="ang"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%C3%A6%C3%BEele#Old_English" class="extiw" title="wikt:æþele">æþele</a></i></i>, for "noble", and <i><i lang="ang"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/r%C3%A6d#Old_English" class="extiw" title="wikt:ræd">ræd</a></i></i>, for "counsel".
</p><p>However, there are also from an early time names which seem to be monothematic, consisting only of a single element. These are sometimes explained as <a href="/wiki/Hypocorism" title="Hypocorism">hypocorisms</a>, short forms of originally dithematic names, but in many cases the etymology of the supposed original name cannot be recovered.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The oldest known Germanic names date to the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a> period, <i><a href="/wiki/Arminius" title="Arminius">Arminius</a></i> and his wife <i><a href="/wiki/Thusnelda" title="Thusnelda">Thusnelda</a></i> in the 1st century, and in greater frequency, especially <a href="/wiki/Gothic_names" class="mw-redirect" title="Gothic names">Gothic names</a>, in the late Roman Empire, in the 4th to 5th centuries (the <a href="/wiki/Germanic_Heroic_Age" title="Germanic Heroic Age">Germanic Heroic Age</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A great variety of names are attested from the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">medieval period</a>, falling into the rough categories of Scandinavian (<a href="/wiki/Old_Norse" title="Old Norse">Old Norse</a>), Anglo-Saxon (<a href="/wiki/Old_English" title="Old English">Old English</a>), continental (<a href="/wiki/Old_Frankish" class="mw-redirect" title="Old Frankish">Frankish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Old_High_German" title="Old High German">Old High German</a> and <a href="/wiki/Low_German" title="Low German">Low German</a>), and <a href="/wiki/East_Germanic_languages" title="East Germanic languages">East Germanic</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Gothic_names" class="mw-redirect" title="Gothic names">Gothic names</a><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>) forms.
By the <a href="/wiki/High_Middle_Ages" title="High Middle Ages">High Middle Ages</a>, many of these names had undergone numerous sound changes and/or were abbreviated, so that their etymology is not always clear.
</p><p>Of the large number of medieval Germanic names, a comparatively small set remains in common use today. The most frequent name of Germanic origin in <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> has traditionally been <a href="/wiki/William_(name)" class="mw-redirect" title="William (name)">William</a> (Bill; from an Old High German Willahelm), followed by <a href="/wiki/Robert" title="Robert">Robert</a> and <a href="/wiki/Charles" title="Charles">Charles</a> (<a href="/wiki/Carl_(name)" title="Carl (name)">Carl</a>, after <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">Charlemagne</a>).
Very few names of native English (Anglo-Saxon) origin survive into current use, the most common of these being <a href="/wiki/Edward" title="Edward">Edward</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edmund_(given_name)" class="mw-redirect" title="Edmund (given name)">Edmund</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edgar_(name)" class="mw-redirect" title="Edgar (name)">Edgar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alfred_(name)" title="Alfred (name)">Alfred</a> and <a href="/wiki/Harold_(given_name)" title="Harold (given name)">Harold</a> for males; the female name <i><a href="/wiki/Audrey" title="Audrey">Audrey</a></i> continues the Anglo-Norman (French) form of the Anglo-Saxon <i><a href="/wiki/%C3%86%C3%B0el%C3%BEry%C3%B0" class="mw-redirect" title="Æðelþryð">Æðelþryð</a></i>.
</p>
<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

<td><i>amala</i></td>
<td>work(?)</td>
<td><img alt="☑" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/20px-Yes_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="20" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/30px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/40px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600" /><span style="display:none">Y</span></td>
<td></td>
<td>Amaleberga, <a href="/wiki/Amalafrida" title="Amalafrida">Amalafrida</a>, Amalrica, <a href="/wiki/Amalaswintha" class="mw-redirect" title="Amalaswintha">Amalaswintha</a>/Melisende/Millicent, <a href="/wiki/Ealhswith" title="Ealhswith">Ealhswith</a></td>
<td>c.f. <a href="/wiki/Amalia_(given_name)" title="Amalia (given name)">Amalia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amelie_(given_name)" class="mw-redirect" title="Amelie (given name)">Amelie</a>. This element's etymology is uncertain, but it is frequently compared to Old Norse <i>aml</i> "work".Note the similarity with Arabic 'عمل' which also means work.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><i>angil, engel; ingal/ingel</i></td>

<td>Burchard/<a href="/wiki/Burchard_(name)" title="Burchard (name)">Burkhart</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burgred" class="mw-redirect" title="Burgred">Burgred</a>; <a href="/wiki/Cuthburh" title="Cuthburh">Cuthburh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eadburh" title="Eadburh">Eadburh</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C3%86thelburh_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Æthelburh (disambiguation)">Æthelburh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Osburh" title="Osburh">Osburh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Redburga" class="mw-redirect" title="Redburga">Redburga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seaxburh" class="mw-disambig" title="Seaxburh">Seaxburh</a>, Walpurga, <a href="/wiki/Werburgh" title="Werburgh">Werburgh</a></td>
<td>The suffix is feminine only. See also <a href="/wiki/Burke" title="Burke">Burke</a>
</td></tr>

<td>honour</td>
<td><img alt="☑" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/20px-Yes_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="20" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/30px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/40px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600" /><span style="display:none">Y</span></td>
<td></td>
<td>Erarich, Eranbald, Erambert, Ernulf</td>
<td>Probably a genuine element, but difficult to distinguish from <i>hari</i>, which is also often reduced to <i>eri-, er-</i>, or from <i>ari, arni</i>. The form <i>erin-</i>, on the other hand,  is often conflated with the <i>irm-</i> element.
</td></tr>

<td><i><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/erchan" class="extiw" title="wikt:erchan">ercan</a>, erchen, archen, eorcen</i></td>
<td>pure, genuine<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup></td>
<td><img alt="☑" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/20px-Yes_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="20" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/30px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/40px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600" /><span style="display:none">Y</span></td>
<td></td>
<td>Ercanberaht/<a href="/wiki/Eorcenberht" class="mw-redirect" title="Eorcenberht">Eorcenberht</a>, Ercanbold/<a href="/wiki/Archibald_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Archibald (disambiguation)">Archibald</a>, Ercamberta, Ercanpurh, Ercantrud, Ercanfrid, Ercangar, Ercanhilt, Erchensinda, Erchanold, Archanolf/Erchenulf</td>
<td>Förstemann, 377 connects OGH <i>ercan</i> "sublime, pure, holy" (the general sense in Gothic as well). In OE and ON used in compounds designating various "precious" stones. Perhaps theophoric, from a name of <a href="/wiki/Teiwaz" class="mw-redirect" title="Teiwaz">Teiwaz</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr>

<td>Erlabald, Erlefrida, Erligar, Erlemund, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Erlwin&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Erlwin (page does not exist)">Erlwin</a>, Erlulf</td>

<td><img alt="☑" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/20px-Yes_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="20" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/30px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/40px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600" /><span style="display:none">Y</span></td>
<td>Gauzebald/Cozpolt/Gausbolda, Gaucibert/Gozperaht, Gauseprand, Gausburgis, Gauttrudis, Caozflat, Gautfred, Gozger, Gauter/Kozheri, Gautastabaz/Göstaf/Gösta/Gustav, Gautshelm, Gauthildis, Gozleih, Gautlindis, <a href="/wiki/Gautrekr" title="Gautrekr">Gautrekr</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goswin_(given_name)" title="Goswin (given name)">Goswin</a>/Gaudoin, Gaudulf; <a href="/wiki/Algaut" title="Algaut">Algaut</a>, Amalgaud, Ansegaud, Ariugaud, <a href="/wiki/Ostrogoth" class="mw-redirect" title="Ostrogoth">Ostgaus</a>/Aostargaoz, Berengaud, Danegaud, Trutgaud, Ebregaud, Ercangaud, Erlegaud, Faregaud, Gisalgoz, Helmigaud, Hildegaud,  Hohgaud,  Hungoz,  Irmegaus, Ermengaud, Teutgaud, Ulgaud,  Waldegaud, Wihgoz, Vuldargoza.</td>
<td>the tribal name of the <a href="/wiki/Geats" title="Geats">Geats</a>/<a href="/wiki/Goths" title="Goths">Goths</a>. Hypocorisms Gaudo, Gaudila, Gauzilin, Gaudin. These names are popular during the 6th to 11th centuries. The forms in <i>got</i> are difficult to distinguish from the element <i>god</i> "god".
</td></tr>

<td>One of the most frequently used stems both as prefix and as suffix, attested since the 3rd century. Among the Franks its use especially for feminine names is "almost excessive" according to Förstemann, who counts 281 names with this suffix, of which only four are masculine. Hypocorism <a href="/wiki/Hilda" title="Hilda">Hilda</a>.

<td><i> hring, ring</i></td>
<td>ring</td>
<td><img alt="☑" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/20px-Yes_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="20" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/30px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/40px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600" /><span style="display:none">Y</span></td>
<td>(?)<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup></td>
<td>Hringuni, Rhincbold, Ringhelm, Hringweald, Hringolf</td>
<td>Förstemann 1900:877 suggests that the "ring" element in origin refers to <a href="/wiki/Chainmail" class="mw-redirect" title="Chainmail">ring-mail</a>

<tr>
<td><i> hroc, roc</i></td>
<td>?</td>
<td><img alt="☑" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/20px-Yes_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="20" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/30px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/40px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600" /><span style="display:none">Y</span></td>
<td><img alt="☑" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/20px-Yes_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="20" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/30px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/40px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600" /><span style="display:none">Y</span></td>
<td>Ferderuchus, Unhroch, Wolfhroc; Rocbert, Hrohhart, Hrocculf, Ruocswint, Berthroc</td>
<td>Förstemann 1900:878f. surmises an early conflation of two elements (1) <i>hrauc</i> "roar, bellow, (battle-)cry" and (2) <i>rōc</i> "care, circumspection", and both were further conflated with <i>hrōþ-</i> as first element, and with <i>-rih</i> as second.  As a second element since the 5th century. <a href="/wiki/Crocus" title="Crocus">Crocus</a>, the 4th-century king of the Alamanni, presumably had a name formed from this element, as did <i>Rocco</i> bishop of Autun (7th century) and  <i>Rocho</i> bishop of Bourges (8th century).
</td></tr>

<td>survivor, heir</td>
<td>(<img alt="☑" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/20px-Yes_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="20" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/30px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/40px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600" /><span style="display:none">Y</span>)</td>
<td><img alt="☑" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/20px-Yes_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="20" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/30px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/40px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600" /><span style="display:none">Y</span></td>
<td>Eggileib, Albleib, <a href="/wiki/Olaf" title="Olaf">Olaf</a>, Oslef, Athulef, Adalleib, Otleib, Berahtleib, Dagalaif, Danleib, Dotleib, Truhtleib, Edilef, Fridaleib, Folkleib, Guntaleiba, Hartleib, Haduleif, <a href="/wiki/Herleif" title="Herleif">Herleif</a>, Hiltileip, Hordleif, Hunleib, Isanleib, Mahtleip, Nordleip, Ortlaip, Ratleib, Reginleib, Richleib, Sileif, Starcleib, <a href="/wiki/Detlef" title="Detlef">Thiotleip</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wiglaf" title="Wiglaf">Wiglaf</a>, Wineleib, Wolleip, Wulfleip, Wunnileif, Zehaleip; Leibuni/Leiboin, Leibher, Leibhilt, Leibrat, Leibwart</td>
<td>the probable original meaning "heir of"  suggests that this element at first appeared only as second element; it was from an early time it conflated with <i>liub</i> "dear". In Old Norse also used as a simplex, <i><a href="/wiki/Leif" title="Leif">Leifr</a></i> "heir".

<td>hypochoristic <a href="/wiki/Wallia" title="Wallia">Wallia</a>, Walica.  c.f. <i><a href="/wiki/Valhalla" title="Valhalla">Valhalla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Valkyrie" title="Valkyrie">Valkyrie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Valf%C3%B6%C3%B0r" class="mw-redirect" title="Valföðr">Valföðr</a></i> etc.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><i>wod</i> (<i>wad</i>?)</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Odhr" class="mw-redirect" title="Odhr">fury</a></td>
<td><img alt="☑" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/20px-Yes_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="20" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/30px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/40px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600" /><span style="display:none">Y</span></td>
<td></td>
<td>Wodilhilt (f.), Wodalgarta (f.), Wodilbalt (a. 969), Wodalbert (a. 773), Wodelfrid (a. 912), Wodilulf (11th century), Vudamot (a. 821)</td>
<td>because of the close association with <a href="/wiki/Wodanaz" class="mw-redirect" title="Wodanaz">Wodanaz</a>, these names are rare already in the OHG period, and fall out of use entirely during the High Middle Ages. Some hypocorisms such as Wote (a. 784), Woda (f., 8th century), Wodal (a. 889), Wode, Wodtke, may derive from this element. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Wotan_(name)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Wotan (name) (page does not exist)">Wotan</a> is recorded as a given name in the early 9th century.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Association of most of these names with <i>wod</i> "fury" is uncertain, as there are the homophonic but unrelated roots of OHG <i>watan</i> "to wade" and <i>wat</i> "garment".<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><i>wid(u), wit</i></td>
<td>wood, forest</td>
<td><img alt="☑" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/20px-Yes_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="20" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/30px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/40px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600" /><span style="display:none">Y</span></td>
<td></td>
<td>Withhold, <a href="/wiki/Widukind" title="Widukind">Widukind</a></td>
<td>hypocorism <a href="/wiki/Guido" title="Guido">Guido</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guy_(given_name)" title="Guy (given name)">Guy</a>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><i><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Appendix:Proto-Germanic/wulfaz" class="extiw" title="wikt:Appendix:Proto-Germanic/wulfaz">wulf</a></i></td>
<td>wolf</td>
<td><img alt="☑" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/20px-Yes_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="20" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/30px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/40px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600" /><span style="display:none">Y</span></td>
<td><img alt="☑" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/20px-Yes_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="20" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/30px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/40px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600" /><span style="display:none">Y</span></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Aethelwulf" class="mw-redirect" title="Aethelwulf">Aethelwulf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beowulf_(hero)" title="Beowulf (hero)">Beowulf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cynewulf" title="Cynewulf">Cynewulf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gangolf" class="mw-redirect" title="Gangolf">Gangolf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gundulf" title="Gundulf">Gundulf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pandulf" class="mw-disambig" title="Pandulf">Pandulf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rudolph_(name)" title="Rudolph (name)">Rudolph</a>; <a href="/wiki/Wulfstan" class="mw-disambig" title="Wulfstan">Wulfstan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Wolfgang (disambiguation)">Wolfgang</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wolfram" class="mw-disambig" title="Wolfram">Wolfram</a>, Wulf (etc.)</td>
<td>Especially as second element,  <i>-ulf</i>, <i>-olf</i> is extremely common. Förstemann explains this as originally motivated by the wolf as an animal sacred to <a href="/wiki/Wodanaz" class="mw-redirect" title="Wodanaz">Wodanaz</a>, but notes that the large number of names indicates that the element had become a meaningless suffix of male names at an early time. Förstemann counts 381 names in  <i>-ulf</i>, <i>-olf</i>, among which only four are feminine.  See also <a href="/wiki/Offa_(name)" class="mw-redirect" title="Offa (name)">Offa (name)</a>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><i>þeod</i></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Theod" class="mw-redirect" title="Theod">people</a></td>
<td><img alt="☑" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/20px-Yes_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="20" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/30px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/40px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600" /><span style="display:none">Y</span></td>
<td></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Theodoric" title="Theodoric">Theodoric</a>/<a href="/wiki/Dietrich_(name)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dietrich (name)">Dietrich</a>/<a href="/wiki/Derick" class="mw-redirect" title="Derick">Derick</a>/<a href="/wiki/Dirk" title="Dirk">Dirk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Detlef" title="Detlef">Detlef</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diether" title="Diether">Diether</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diethelm_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Diethelm (disambiguation)">Diethelm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Theobald_(name)" class="mw-redirect" title="Theobald (name)">Theobald</a>,  Dietfried, Theudebert, <a href="/wiki/Theodemar" class="mw-redirect" title="Theodemar">Theodemar</a>; Dietlinde
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><i>*þegnaz</i>, <i><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Degen#Etymology_1" class="extiw" title="wikt:Degen">degen</a></i></td>
<td>warrior, <a href="/wiki/Thegn" title="Thegn">thane</a></td>
<td><img alt="☑" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/20px-Yes_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="20" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/30px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/40px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600" /><span style="display:none">Y</span></td>
<td><img alt="☑" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/20px-Yes_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="20" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/30px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/40px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600" /><span style="display:none">Y</span></td>
<td>Degenhard, Degericus; Deitdegen, Edildegan,  Drûtdegan,  Heridegan,  Swertdegan, Volcdegen
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><i>þryþ,</i>
<p>OH <i>þrúðr,</i> OE <i>þrȳð,</i><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> 
<i>drut, trud, thrud, thryth</i> 
</p>
</td>
<td>force, strength</td>
<td><img alt="☑" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/20px-Yes_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="20" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/30px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/40px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600" /><span style="display:none">Y</span></td>
<td><img alt="☑" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/20px-Yes_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="20" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/30px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/40px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600" /><span style="display:none">Y</span></td>
<td>Drutmund; <a href="/wiki/%C3%86thelthryth" title="Æthelthryth">Æthelthryth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Osthryth" title="Osthryth">Osthryth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cynethryth" title="Cynethryth">Cynethryth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ermintrude" class="mw-redirect" title="Ermintrude">Ermintrude</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gertrude_(given_name)" title="Gertrude (given name)">Gertrude</a>, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A6thryth" title="Sæthryth">Sæthryth</a>, Waltrud/Waltraut</td>
<td>Names with this suffix are feminine only; <a href="/wiki/%C3%9Er%C3%BA%C3%B0r" title="Þrúðr">Þrúðr</a> is a daughter of Thor in Norse mythology. Short form <a href="/wiki/Trudy_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Trudy (disambiguation)">Trudy, Trudi</a>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><i>þonar, donar, þór</i></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Thor" title="Thor">(the god of) thunder</a></td>
<td><img alt="☑" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/20px-Yes_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="20" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/30px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/40px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600" /><span style="display:none">Y</span></td>
<td>(rare)</td>
<td>Donarperht (9th century), Donarad (8th century), Þórarin, Þórhall, <a href="/wiki/Thorkel" title="Thorkel">Þórkell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thorfinn_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Thorfinn (disambiguation)">Þórfinnr</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thorvald" title="Thorvald">Þórvald</a>,  Þórvarðr, Þórgeir, <a href="/wiki/Thorsten" title="Thorsten">Þórsteinn</a> (9th century), Thunerulf/<a href="/wiki/Thorolf" title="Thorolf">Þórolf</a>&#160;; Albthonar (8th century)</td>
<td>These names appear from the 8th or 9th century; popular in Scandinavia during the 10th to 11th centuries. Förstemann 1199.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><i>þurs, Thuris, Turis</i></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/J%C3%B6tunn" title="Jötunn">giant</a></td>
<td><img alt="☑" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/20px-Yes_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="20" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/30px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/40px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600" /><span style="display:none">Y</span></td>
<td></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Thusnelda" title="Thusnelda">Thusnelda</a> (1st century; presumably for *Thurishilda), Thurismund (6th century), <a href="/wiki/Thurisind" title="Thurisind">Thurisind</a> (6th century), Turisulfus</td>
<td>an archaic element in names of the migration period, extinct during the medieval period.  Förstemann 1200.
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><br />
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Monothematic_names">Monothematic names</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Germanic_name&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Monothematic names">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Some medieval Germanic names are attested in simplex form; these names originate as <a href="/wiki/Hypocorism" title="Hypocorism">hypocorisms</a> of full dithematic names, but in some cases they entered common usage and were no longer perceived as such.
</p>
<ul><li>Masculine: Aldo (whence English Aldous), <a href="/wiki/Adel_(name)" title="Adel (name)">Adel</a>, Anso,  Anzo/Enzo, Folki/Folke/Fulco, Gero, Helmo, Ise/Iso, Kuno, Lanzo, Manno, Odo/<a href="/wiki/Otto" title="Otto">Otto</a>, Rocco, <a href="/wiki/Sten_(name)" title="Sten (name)">Sten</a>, Waldo, Warin, Wido, Wine, Wolf/Wulf</li>
<li>Feminine: <a href="/wiki/Adele_(given_name)" title="Adele (given name)">Adele</a>, Alda, <a href="/wiki/Bertha" title="Bertha">Bertha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emma_(given_name)" title="Emma (given name)">Emma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hilda_(name)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hilda (name)">Hilda</a>, Ida, Isa, <a href="/wiki/Linda_(name)" class="mw-redirect" title="Linda (name)">Linda</a>, Oda</li></ul>
<p>Some hypocorisms retain a remnant of their second element, but reduced so that it cannot be identified unambiguously any longer; Curt/Kurt may abbreviate either Conrad or Cunibert. Harry may abbreviate either Harold or Henry.
</p><p>Other monothematic names originate as surnames (bynames) rather than hypocorism of old dithematic names. E.g. Old English
Æsc "ash tree", <a href="/wiki/Carl_(name)" title="Carl (name)">Carl</a> "free man" (<a href="/wiki/Charles" title="Charles">Charles</a>), <a href="/wiki/Hengest" class="mw-redirect" title="Hengest">Hengest</a> "stallion", Raban "raven" (<a href="/wiki/Rabanus_Maurus" title="Rabanus Maurus">Rabanus Maurus</a>), Hagano/<a href="/wiki/Hagen" title="Hagen">Hagen</a> "enclosure", <a href="/wiki/Ernest" title="Ernest">Earnest</a> "vigorous, resolute".
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Uncertain_etymology">Uncertain etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Germanic_name&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Uncertain etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Gustav_(name)" title="Gustav (name)">Gustav</a> has been interpreted by e.g. Elof Hellquist (1864 - 1939) Swedish linguist specialist in North Germanic languages as <i>gauta-stabaz</i> (gauta-stabaR) "staff of the <a href="/wiki/Geat" class="mw-redirect" title="Geat">Geats</a>"; it may also originate as an adaptation of the Slavic name <i>Gostislav</i>.</li>
<li>Old English Pǣga (unknown meaning)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pippin_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Pippin (disambiguation)">Pepin</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Serlo_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Serlo (disambiguation)">Serlo</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Morcar" title="Morcar">Morcar</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Zotto" title="Zotto">Zotto</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Zaban" title="Zaban">Zaban</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cleph" title="Cleph">Cleph</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pemmo_of_Friuli" title="Pemmo of Friuli">Pemmo</a></li></ul>

.cs1-visible-error{font-size:100%}.mw-parser-output .cs1-maint{display:none;color:#33aa33;margin-left:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .cs1-subscription,.mw-parser-output .cs1-registration,.mw-parser-output .cs1-format{font-size:95%}.mw-parser-output .cs1-kern-left,.mw-parser-output .cs1-kern-wl-left{padding-left:0.2em}.mw-parser-output .cs1-kern-right,.mw-parser-output .cs1-kern-wl-right{padding-right:0.2em}</style> and <cite class="citation book">Förstemann, Ernst (1900). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://sul-derivatives.stanford.edu/derivative?CSNID=00003871&amp;mediaType=application/pdf"><i>Altdeutsches Namenbuch</i></a> (3 ed.). Bonn: P. Hanstein.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Altdeutsches+Namenbuch&amp;rft.place=Bonn&amp;rft.edition=3&amp;rft.pub=P.+Hanstein&amp;rft.date=1900&amp;rft.aulast=F%C3%B6rstemann&amp;rft.aufirst=Ernst&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fsul-derivatives.stanford.edu%2Fderivative%3FCSNID%3D00003871%26mediaType%3Dapplication%2Fpdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGermanic+name" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-4">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://indo-european.info/pokorny-etymological-dictionary/ank-1.htm">"ank-1"</a>. <i>indo-european.info</i>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=indo-european.info&amp;rft.atitle=ank-1&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Findo-european.info%2Fpokorny-etymological-dictionary%2Fank-1.htm&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGermanic+name" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-5">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">c.f. OE <i><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/ehtan" class="extiw" title="wikt:ehtan">ehtan</a></i></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-6">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://indo-european.info/pokorny-etymological-dictionary/agh.htm">"agh-"</a>. <i>indo-european.info</i>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=indo-european.info&amp;rft.atitle=agh-&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Findo-european.info%2Fpokorny-etymological-dictionary%2Fagh.htm&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGermanic+name" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-7"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-7">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">names terminating in <i>-ald</i> are from <i>-wald</i>.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-8"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-8">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Vestralpus" title="Vestralpus">Vestralpus</a>, the name of an Alamannic king, may be a rare instance of this element occurring in the second part of a name.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-aelsinus-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-aelsinus_9-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-aelsinus_9-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">attested as latinized <a href="/wiki/%C3%86lsinus" title="Ælsinus">Ælsinus</a></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-10"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-10">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">perhaps reduced from  Ælfgifu, or  Ælthelgifu.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-11"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-11">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">this name survives in corrupted form in the given name <a href="/wiki/Axel_(name)" title="Axel (name)">Axel</a> and in the surnames Aslock, Hasluck</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-12"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-12">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">some possible rare exceptions, such as Fulcarb.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-13"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-13">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">often conflated with Latin Pilgrim, Peregrinus</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-14"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-14">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">perhaps as a suffix in certain names latinized as <i>-domus</i>.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-15"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-15">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">c.f. Old English <i>eorcnan-stan</i> "precious stone, gem". <a href="/wiki/IEW" class="mw-redirect" title="IEW">Pokorny (1959)</a> tentatively grouped the word with <a href="/wiki/PIE_root" class="mw-redirect" title="PIE root">PIE</a> <i>*arǵ-</i> "glittering, shining", whence Latin <i>argentum</i> "silver"), but Gothic <i>ark-</i> may also represent an early loan from Greek ἀρχι- ("<a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/arch-" class="extiw" title="wikt:arch-">arch-</a>", c.f. Ulfilan Gothic <i>arkaggilus</i> for  <i><a href="/wiki/Archangel" title="Archangel">archangelus</a></i>). Formerly (Diefenbach 1851) also compared to Sanskrit <i>arh-</i> "to be worthy".</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-16"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-16">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i><a href="/wiki/Ear_(rune)" title="Ear (rune)">Erchtag</a></i> was a name of Tuesday in Bavarian dialect; see Grimm, <i><a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Mythologie" title="Deutsche Mythologie">Deutsche Mythologie</a></i>, 113; 182—185.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-ferdinand-17"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-ferdinand_17-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-ferdinand_17-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">apparently a Gothic name; perhaps from <i>fardi</i> "travel" (Förstemann, 401), perhaps also from <i>frithu</i> "protection".</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-:0-18"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-:0_18-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-:0_18-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Okasha, Elisabeth (2016-12-05). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=jQKoDQAAQBAJ&amp;printsec=frontcover#v=snippet&amp;q=fri%C3%BE"><i>Women's Names in Old English</i></a>. Routledge. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9781351871211" title="Special:BookSources/9781351871211"><bdi>9781351871211</bdi></a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Women%27s+Names+in+Old+English&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.date=2016-12-05&amp;rft.isbn=9781351871211&amp;rft.aulast=Okasha&amp;rft.aufirst=Elisabeth&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DjQKoDQAAQBAJ%26printsec%3Dfrontcover%23v%3Dsnippet%26q%3Dfri%25C3%25BE&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGermanic+name" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-19"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-19">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">perhaps conflated with <i>hild-</i> from an early time.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-20"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-20">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">names with this second element have been conflated with names in <i>-rad</i>. Förstemann 1900:875.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-21"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-21">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">names with this second element are uncertain, most of the candidates could contain the simple suffix <i>-ing</i>. Förstemann 1900:877.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-22"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-22">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Lena Peterson <i>Nordiskt runnamnslexikon</i> (2002)</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-23"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-23">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">cognate to Old Irish <i>néit</i> "combat", see <a href="/wiki/Pokorny_(1959)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pokorny (1959)">Pokorny (1959)</a>, p. 755.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-24"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-24">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Yonge, p. 306.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-25"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-25">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">see Hellmut Rosenfeld, <i>Der Name Wieland</i>, Beiträge zur Namenforschung (1969)</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-26"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-26">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Förstemann, 1332f.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-27"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-27">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Förstemann, 1224.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-28"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-28">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.nordicnames.de/wiki/%C3%9ERU%C3%90">"ÞRUÐ - Nordic Names Wiki - Name Origin, Meaning and Statistics"</a>. <i>www.nordicnames.de</i><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2017-01-31</span></span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=www.nordicnames.de&amp;rft.atitle=%C3%9ERU%C3%90+-+Nordic+Names+Wiki+-+Name+Origin%2C+Meaning+and+Statistics&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.nordicnames.de%2Fwiki%2F%25C3%259ERU%25C3%2590&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGermanic+name" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
